[2026-01-24T23:29:39Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: Q.	Václav Havel was a X dissident when this country was ruled by a puppet regime allied with the Soviet Union. In 1978, he wrote the essay “The Power of the Powerless.” In it, he talks about a greengrocer who puts a sign in his shop window that says “workers of the world, unite!”, which is a quote from the book Y. Havel wrote that we can safely assume that the overwhelming majority of shopkeepers never think about the slogans that they put in their windows, nor do they use them to express their real opinions. With this parable, Havel explained how authoritarian regimes endure not just through repression but also through routine acts of compliance by citizens. He called this kind of outward conformance with the system’s rituals, slogans, and behaviors “A within the B.” He then argued that the solution to this would be for ordinary people to start “A in C” to puncture the narratives of the system and make it clear to other people that they all don’t believe them. ID X, Y, A, B, and C. B and C are antonyms.
